  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2aee3f5c-4d6c-4c28-9249-fb20bfc961df'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7290066-joseph-ribera"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1325293018i/7290066._UX100_CR0,11,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7290066-joseph-ribera">Joseph Ribera</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">In my opinion the book is more suitable for 13 and older. I read it as a senior, but in the original Spanish. While it delves into fantasy it also dea<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">In my opinion the book is more suitable for 13 and older. I read it as a senior, but in the original Spanish. While it delves into fantasy it also deals with adult subjects, ecological science, mythology, and human and animal rights. I think it is a great YA book, but in the original is also a good book for adults studying Spanish who are at an intermediate (B1) level.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <span id="freeText17468294757654882720" style="display:none">La ciudad de las bestias = City of the Beasts (Memories of the Eagle and the Jaguar #1), Isabel Allende<br /><br /><b>City of the Beasts</b> is the first young adult novel by Chilean-American writer Isabel Allende. Published in 2002. <br /><br /><b>City of the Beasts</b> begins with the story of Alexander Cold, who is 15 years old and going through a family crisis. While his parents leave for Texas to try to treat his mother's cancer, Alex and his sisters are sent to live with their grandmothers. Despite his desperate pleading, Alex is sent off to New York City to stay with his eccentric grandmother Kate Cold, a reporter for International Geographic Magazine. His sisters, however are sent to live with their Grandmother Carla. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Kate announces that she will be taking Alex with her to the Amazon rain-forest during his visit. Once Alex arrives in New York City, and finds out that his grandmother had no intentions of collecting him at the airport and is forced to walk to her apartment, several blocks away. In the process he meets a girl named Morgana, a homeless girl in her mid-20's. <br /><br />She offers him pot and steals his backpack that contained his clothes, his money and his flute. He is greatly saddened by the loss of his precious flute, but Kate gives him the flute belonging to his grandfather, Joseph Cold. Soon, they pack off to go to the Amazon with some professors and photographers. The reason Kate goes is to write an article about the Beast. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز ششم ماه آگوست سال 2011میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: اشباح مه کتاب دوم از سه گانه عقاب و جاگوار؛ نویسنده: ایزابل آلنده؛ مترجم آسیه عزیزی؛ پروانه عزیزی؛ تهران، اندیشه سازان، 1389؛ در 331ص؛ <br /><br />عنوان: شهر جانوران کتاب دوم از سه گانه عقاب و جاگوار؛ نویسنده: ایزابل آلنده؛ مترجم: اسدالله امرایی؛ تهران، تندیس، 1383؛ در 332ص؛ شابک 9789645757838؛ چاپ دوم 1389؛<br /><br />ایزابل آلنده، در رمان: شهر جانوران؛ داستان نوجوانی به نام: «آلکساندر کولد» را، روایت می‌کند، که به علت بیماری مادر خویش، نزد مادربزرگ پدری‌ خویش، می‌رود، اما در نیویورک، و پیش از رسیدن به خانه ی مادربزرگ، پول و وسایل او را می‌دزدند؛ مادربزرگ، زنی مهربان، و در عین حال یک‌دنده است، که روش تعلیم و تربیت ویژه ی خود را دارد.مادر آلکس سرطان دارد، و تحت شیمی‌ درمانی، قرار گرفته، مادربزرگ نویسنده است، و ماموریت گرفته، برای پژوهش و نوشتن مقاله‌ ای درباره جانورانی عظیم‌ الجثه، به امریکای جنوبی برود، و در مورد علت مرگ و میر بومیان پژوهش کند ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14907466986564172733">Gah! I was really disappointed with this little series from Allende. I love her books so much, but she did NOT successfully make the transition to writing for younger readers. The plots of all three in the series were very interesting and could have been a lot of fun, but the writing was often awkward and forced, especially the magical bits. The characters were a little two-dimensional, and even the dialogue was strained. She had some nifty ideas, but it seemed like she was trying to dumb them d</span>
  <span id="freeText14907466986564172733" style="display:none">Gah! I was really disappointed with this little series from Allende. I love her books so much, but she did NOT successfully make the transition to writing for younger readers. The plots of all three in the series were very interesting and could have been a lot of fun, but the writing was often awkward and forced, especially the magical bits. The characters were a little two-dimensional, and even the dialogue was strained. She had some nifty ideas, but it seemed like she was trying to dumb them down for younger readers, rather than just letting them flow. </span>

<div id="review_2046769549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2046769549" />
    <a title="Michelle Curie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27203016-michelle-curie"><img alt="Michelle Curie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600963618p2/27203016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2046769549?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Curie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Curie" href="/user/show/27203016-michelle-curie">Michelle Curie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007146376" href="/book/show/149169.City_of_the_Beasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27203016-michelle-curie?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27203016-michelle-curie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2046769549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6585347807942936476"><b>
  <i>"The longer I live, the more uninformed I feel. Only the young have an explanation for everything."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I saw this book lurking in my bookshelf the other day and a sense of nostalgia swept over me as I remembered how this might have been one of the first <i>Young Adult</i> books I've ever read, all the way back when I wasn't even one myself. I picked this up again, wondering how well I remembered things and how I perceived them now. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499064721i/23186669.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In this Amazonian adventure, fifteen year old Alexander Cold is sent ou</span>
  <span id="freeText6585347807942936476" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"The longer I live, the more uninformed I feel. Only the young have an explanation for everything."</i>
</b><br><br>I saw this book lurking in my bookshelf the other day and a sense of nostalgia swept over me as I remembered how this might have been one of the first <i>Young Adult</i> books I've ever read, all the way back when I wasn't even one myself. I picked this up again, wondering how well I remembered things and how I perceived them now. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499064721i/23186669.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In this Amazonian adventure, fifteen year old Alexander Cold is sent out to his grandmother Kate, as his mother is struggling with cancer at home, too weak to look after him. Kate is a fearless reporter about to embark on an International Geographic expedition to the dangerous, remote world of the Amazon rainforest, on which Alexander now has to join her. The mission to document the legendary beast of the Amazon turns out to be a hard one, with many hidden secrets and dangers lurking, as Alex and his new friend Nadia soon discover. <br><br>The fact that this has been describes as an <i>ecological romance</i> makes me cringe, as this is definitely neither a flattering nor an accurate way to describe this. In fact, part of why I enjoyed reading this was because it wasn't a romance story - it's an adventure. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499064721i/23186671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isabel Allende created some wonderful characters here - the participants of the expedition all got their unique character traits, they're dynamic feels real and believable and I particularly liked how tough the females in this story were. They're definitely victims to men who think themselves as authoritarian, but at the same time they're in no way afraid to stand their ground. Our main characters are young adults - we've got the 15 year old Alexander and the 13 year old Nadia and both of them felt believable as well. They're hitting puberty, where you might feel in charge and in control of everything, but at the same time you're clearly not. Still, they're never annoying, but ultimately good-natured and brave kids. <br><br>In terms of themes, they were a lot of messages conveyed that I certainly didn't pick up on as a kid. Allende explores the contrast between our civilisation and nature as well as the exploitation of native cultures and does both in a elegantly subtle way. I feel like <i>elegant</i> is a good word to describe her writing in general, it's vivid, gentle and descriptive and I could so clearly visualise everything that was happening. <br><br>In general, I am absolutely aware that age-wise this book is not targeted at me, which makes me put it in a different context and influences my expectations, but it's still an enjoyable tale!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6585347807942936476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13150804579106545347">Honestly, this book sucked. Majorly. Giving it two stars was generous, to say the least.<br/>The beginning was boring beyond belief. I had to read this for school, and my class and I begged the teacher to let us read another one. It had no interest for us, no appeal.   <span id="freeText13150804579106545347" style="display:none">Honestly, this book sucked. Majorly. Giving it two stars was generous, to say the least.<br />The beginning was boring beyond belief. I had to read this for school, and my class and I begged the teacher to let us read another one. It had no interest for us, no appeal. I hated the grandmother, didn't know what to think of the main character, and was bored out of my mind by the language. When the main character was swimming with the dolphins, the story basically went, 'I was having so much fun. It was the best day of my life.', and then boom, on to the next boring-as-crap thing. I had to wonder if something was lost in the translation... The first half of the book had a snails pace, just prolonging our torture.<br />The second half of the book picked up a LITTLE! It had a bit more magic and fantasy, a bit more interesting stuff going on. But I was still prevented from even beginning to enjoy this book because of the lack of descriptive language.<br />I just hated this book. I would never in a billion years recommend it to anyone but my worst enemy. Maybe not even then.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13642708598153104896">When I first got that book for Christmas (and in german) a couple years ago, I really didn't knew if I should like it.   <span id="freeText13642708598153104896" style="display:none">When I first got that book for Christmas (and in german) a couple years ago, I really didn't knew if I should like it. At that time I did not liked reading that much. But it was a present, so I started it. And couldn't stop! I loved it. The way Isabel Allende made it so understandable how life in a Rain forest could be, and is. It is truly amazing. The story of Nadja and Alexander, how they became best friends and thought they would never see each other again after that miraculous adventure - fascinating. The only think I was really sad about is the part in the mountain. <br />The intoxicating plot of the main characters is opening with Alexander and the story how he came to his Grandmothers Apartment without money in NYC and why he came at all. His family is hit with illness and without ideas how to fix it they try everything. One of them is that the male Main Character is leaving with his Grandmother to the Southern American Jungle. What he doesn't know at that time is that he finds more than just a cure for his mother. He is finding himself and his totemic animal, his best friend, and the journey of his life. As soon as they touch down in Manaus he is also overwhelmed with the heat of south America. Soon he was about to meet the young Nadja, at the age of his annoying little sister, so it is wierd for him to be around her at first. But Nadja is much mature at the same age. The young soon-to-be-friends are about to start a expedition with a team of Journalists (Alex's Grandmother) and Photographers and so on. Nadjas Father is the guide for the expedition. The team is standing out to more than just one challenge and is supposed to find animals who are probably older than any human ever remembered. Within that journey both of the teens are reaching over their biggest fears and exploring new territory in their minds and untouched earth.</span>

<div id="review_23503377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23503377" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1117991-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209204542p2/1117991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23503377?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/1117991-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23503377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7632658629753820790">I wanted to try some of Allende's work, and being lazy I picked one of her kids' books. However, I'm not sure that was the best choice after all. 'City of the Beasts' was not quite my cup of tea, even though I generally enjoy YA-books. However, I tend to enjoy them because they are lighthearted and easy to read, or because they present difficult problems in a slightly less depressing light. City on the Beasts did not have that lightness. It wanted to incorporate some issues (genocide, exploitati</span>
  <span id="freeText7632658629753820790" style="display:none">I wanted to try some of Allende's work, and being lazy I picked one of her kids' books. However, I'm not sure that was the best choice after all. 'City of the Beasts' was not quite my cup of tea, even though I generally enjoy YA-books. However, I tend to enjoy them because they are lighthearted and easy to read, or because they present difficult problems in a slightly less depressing light. City on the Beasts did not have that lightness. It wanted to incorporate some issues (genocide, exploitation of native cultures, the damage that is done to some parts of the earth), but I felt it got a bit preachy at times. Too many issues presented in far too simple terms. Good and evil were a bit too clearly separated, there was only one morally ambiguous character (Leblanc) and he basically turned from caricature annoyingness to not very believable okayness in one moment. Didn't work for me. Also, there was a plot-twist at the end that I found very very very predictable.<br /><br />Still, three stars for the nice writing and some things that I really liked reading about, even though I didn't think they were altogether believable. In addition, some parts of the book were rather suspenseful, which is why I kept on reading until the end.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7632658629753820790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16680018257799059701">My friend read Isabel Allende books and she lend me this one. At first, after a few pages, I was sceptical and didn't expect much. I decided to keep on reading in any case (I cannot put a book down, even if it is bad) and I soon relized that I may have been predjudiced. <br/><br/>The story line was quite nice but the fact that the boy played flute certainly made an impact.   <span id="freeText16680018257799059701" style="display:none">My friend read Isabel Allende books and she lend me this one. At first, after a few pages, I was sceptical and didn't expect much. I decided to keep on reading in any case (I cannot put a book down, even if it is bad) and I soon relized that I may have been predjudiced. <br /><br />The story line was quite nice but the fact that the boy played flute certainly made an impact. I had some trouble with my commitment towards my flute playing because I didn't practice and whatever. Although him pulling his flute out and playing in the Amazon seems a bit well crazy and far-fetched it really made me want to play flute. <br /><br />So this book brought my passion back for my lovely flute. I think overall there are some real inspirational thoughts and moral values portrayed in this book in an easy, understandable way. I would recommend this to everyone, even thos who do not like to read. It's an easy read with passion and adventure (what more od you need?).</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=young-and-new-adult-fairy-tales">young-and-new-adult-fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315949933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17892513183240417755">This is really like Indy Jones, though unlike her adult books, Allende tells too much instead of showing.<br/><br/><br/>What is interesting about this book is the amount of background as well as action Allende packs into the book. During the journey in the Amazon, the characters of both Alex and Nadia are totally real as are most of the supporting characters. A good quick read for an adult</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528416262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2309274427477039941">I have to admit that till I reached the half of the book I was quite skeptic. I thought it was the classic story about children winning in some ways against insensible adults. In the beginning actually the story is a bit disconnected in my opinion. There were a lot informations and too much on the plate. I couldn't find the purpose, the real starting point. But when I reached the third to last chapter I understood everything, all the doubts, troubles, characters, dialogues. Everything came up cl</span>
  <span id="freeText2309274427477039941" style="display:none">I have to admit that till I reached the half of the book I was quite skeptic. I thought it was the classic story about children winning in some ways against insensible adults. In the beginning actually the story is a bit disconnected in my opinion. There were a lot informations and too much on the plate. I couldn't find the purpose, the real starting point. But when I reached the third to last chapter I understood everything, all the doubts, troubles, characters, dialogues. Everything came up clear. All the words that Isabel uses have a precise aim. There is this particular that made me completely change my mind about the book: when Nadia and Alex return from the volcano and reunite with the rest of the group, it was like only with the use of adjectives, that apparently seem without profit, she clearly make them and me too understand the reality and the truth.<br />So in the end I have to say that this book is a revelation and I absolutely recommended it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2309274427477039941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer348819713&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348819713" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16118714704412105815">Beginning<br/> <br/>City of the Beasts begins with the story of Alexander Cold, who is 15 years old and going through a family crisis. While his parents leave for Texas to try to treat his mother's cancer, Alex and his sisters are sent to live with their grandmothers. Despite his desperate pleading, Alex is sent off to New York City to stay with his eccentric grandmother Kate Cold,a reporter for International Geographic Magazine. His sisters, however are sent to live with their Grandmother Carla. Meanwhil</span>
  <span id="freeText16118714704412105815" style="display:none">Beginning<br /> <br />City of the Beasts begins with the story of Alexander Cold, who is 15 years old and going through a family crisis. While his parents leave for Texas to try to treat his mother's cancer, Alex and his sisters are sent to live with their grandmothers. Despite his desperate pleading, Alex is sent off to New York City to stay with his eccentric grandmother Kate Cold,a reporter for International Geographic Magazine. His sisters, however are sent to live with their Grandmother Carla. Meanwhile, Kate announces that she will be taking Alex with her to the Amazon rainforest during his visit. Once Alex arrives in New York City, and finds out that his grandmother had no intentions of collecting him at the airport and is forced to walk to her apartment, several blocks away. In the process he meets a girl named Morgana who is a very eccentric girl in her mid-20s. She steals his back pack that contained his clothes, his money and his flute. He is greatly saddened by the loss of his precious flute, but Kate gives him the flute belonging to his grandfather, Joseph Cold.<br /> <br />[edit] Arrival at the Amazon<br /> <br />When Alex and his Grandmother Kate reach the jungle, they join the rest of the expedition group: Timothy Bruce (photographer); and his assistant Joel Gonzalez. Accompanying them is the famous anthropologist, Ludovic Leblanc, the beautiful Venezuelan physician Dr. Omayra Torres, who is coming along to vaccinate natives, and Cesar Santos, their Brazilian guide. Alex soon befriends Nadia, a girl several years younger than him, who is the daughter of Cesar Santos. The entrepreneur, Mauro Carias, is the man responsible for drawing the magazine's interest to the mysterious Beasts.<br /> <br />[edit] The Expedition<br /> <br />The group leaves by boat, traveling upriver toward their destination in the World's Eye. Everyone in the group feels uncomfortable, as if someone were watching them constantly. One of the soldiers who is with them dies when he is shot by a poisoned dart. Later, Joel Gonzalez, the photographer's assistant, is attacked and nearly killed by an anaconda. After another soldier's death, this time at the hands of a Beast, they decide to send several people back with the wounded Joel Gonzalez - and they are given the task to send help back to the expedition.<br /> <br />When they are left alone, Alex plays his grandfather's flute to relieve the tedium. The music attracts the mysterious People of the Mist, who kidnap the two children. They travel farther into the forest and arrive at a waterfall which they must climb to reach the World's Eye. Due to Alex's skills in rock climbing, this isn't much of a problem for him; however, Nadia is afraid of heights. After they reach the top, Alex is sent back down again to rescue their chief, Mokarita, who had fallen and been mortally wounded. When everyone arrives at the top, they set off for the home of the People of the Mist.<br /> <br />[edit] The People of the Mist<br /> <br />When they reach the village, they are welcomed by the Indians - but their happiness is tempered by the death of Mokarita, which follows shortly after. He is given a traditional funeral, which unfortunately sends up a great amount of smoke from the pyre. During the funeral, everyone is given a drug which reveals to Nadia her totem of the eagle. Jaguar and Eagle are initiated into the clan. Alex, being fifteen, is put through a rite of passage into manhood; during the ceremony, unusual things happen. Firstly, he turns into a jaguar, his totem; secondly, he receives a vision of his mom in the game is on her hospital bed and talking briefly with her. After the ceremonies, the Shaman takes them to visit the Beasts, who live in a city deep within the forest. These Beasts are considered gods by the People of the Mist. Jaguar correctly assumes their city to be the famous El Dorado which is really made from fool's gold. Jaguar and Eagle embark on a journey to visit El Dorado and its inhabitants with the help of Walimai, the mystic's spirit wife who will serve as their guide. The city is located inside of an inactive volcano, and the only entrance is through a confusing labyrinth of lava tunnels and caves. They all decide what to do and how to do it.<br /> <br />[edit] The Beasts of the Amazon<br /> <br />Upon arrival, Alex and Nadia meet with the “Beasts”. The creatures, which look something like giant sloths, function as the living memory of the tribe by remembering long epic poems recited by Walimai and his predecessors. Fearing the capture of these ancient creatures by western scientists, they warn them to be careful of foreigners (such as the expedition group they both belonged to). In exchange for protecting them, the two children ask for gifts: Nadia the "crystal eggs" and Alex the water of life to save his mother. They both manage to get them, but only by giving up that which was really important to them. Nadia gives up the protective necklace given to her by Walimai, and Alex gives up the flute given to him. Upon returning to the village, they discover that it has been taken over by the Expedition, Carias, and Ariosto. After Nadia convinces the Indians to receive vaccinations, the children realize that the vaccines are actually deadly doses of the measles virus, part of Carias's plan to destroy the Amazonian Indians. Karakawe, an expedition member, is revealed to be an officer of the Department for the Protection of Indigenous Peoples; he is shot by Ariosto. The Indians flee into the woods as a full-fledged gunfight breaks out. Luckily, it ends quickly. Ariosto and his soldiers take captive all of the members of the expedition, while Carias (who was given a serious head wound during the fighting) is airlifted to a hospital. The two children manage to escape; the rest of the men are knocked unconscious by the smell of one of the Beasts. Ariosto is knocked out by the stench and then killed by the Beast. After the People of the Mist reach an agreement with the remaining members of the expedition (they will protect that area with all the power, influence, and money they can muster), they leave.<br /> <br />[edit] Ending<br /> <br />In the end, Eagle and Jaguar must part. She gives Alex the three "crystal eggs", which turn out to be giant diamonds. With the money gained from their sale, it was hoped that they would be able to fund a foundation to keep the World's Eye safe. Alex tells her that the best thing about the trip was meeting her, and they agree that they will be best friends forever.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16118714704412105815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1969219677" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969219677" />
    <a title="ReaderSP" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13729798-readersp"><img alt="ReaderSP" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598323408p2/13729798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1969219677?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ReaderSP" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ReaderSP" href="/user/show/13729798-readersp">ReaderSP</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22042530-city-of-the-beasts">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969219677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2230108294592356285">I had heard of this author but had never read any of her books until a friend was telling me about a fantastic book he was reading (City of the Beasts) and I realised that I had added it to my Kindle some time ago, meaning to read it but never had, so I started it straight away. <br/><br/>We follow Alex Cold as he is sent off to stay with his fierce, eccentric grandmother Kate whilst his mother is in hospital with cancer. Kate is just about to set off on a journey to the far reaches of the Amazon rainfore</span>
  <span id="freeText2230108294592356285" style="display:none">I had heard of this author but had never read any of her books until a friend was telling me about a fantastic book he was reading (City of the Beasts) and I realised that I had added it to my Kindle some time ago, meaning to read it but never had, so I started it straight away. <br /><br />We follow Alex Cold as he is sent off to stay with his fierce, eccentric grandmother Kate whilst his mother is in hospital with cancer. Kate is just about to set off on a journey to the far reaches of the Amazon rainforest with a group from International Geographic magazine so Alex joins her. The party is trying to hunt down a fearsome 'beast' that has been roaming the area and when they meet with the rest of the expedition it becomes apparent that the leader of the party, Ludovic Le Blanc, is not happy to see an extra member of their group in the form of a 15-year-old American schoolboy. This situation is made worse for Le Blanc with the addition of Nadia, their guide’s daughter. But both children join the expedition and the group set off. <br /><br />It’s hard to explain the plot without giving too much away but what follows is the start of a powerful friendship between Nadia and Alex and an out-of-this-world adventure. At various points we encounter murder, kidnap, shamans, ghosts, prehistoric creatures, lies, deceit and mysterious and mythical creatures. The Amazon setting allows for fantastic descriptions of the environment. We see photographers attacked by caimans, macaws screeching in the tree tops and dolphins swimming alongside the boats...all the colours, sounds, smells, humidity and incredible sights burst out of this book's pages and create a fantastic atmosphere for the reader. <br /><br />The characters are well formed and the storyline is clear and interesting. I did find some scenes or character actions a little childish but this is a YA book, so it should be expected. As I said, the descriptions of the atmosphere and journey are very well written and draw the reader into the adventure with the characters.<br /><br />I have learnt that Isabel Allende is a fantastic storyteller. This book is a fairytale, pure escapist fiction that, if you have a good imagination and like to drift off into the realms of fantasy, captures you and carries you off into its amazing world. If, however, you prefer more ‘realist’ fiction then it is probably not for you - which is probably why I struggled slightly when I got about 2/3rds through the story. Although this is a fairytale, we cannot fail to notice the underlying thought-provoking comment on society and what we have done to indigenous tribes everywhere. Overall, I enjoyed the book but will not rush out straight away to read the other 2 books in the trilogy. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2230108294592356285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2633919620" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2633919620" />
    <a title="Berenike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19388647-berenike"><img alt="Berenike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557764139p2/19388647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2633919620?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Berenike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berenike" href="/user/show/19388647-berenike">Berenike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788484411666" href="/book/show/67661.La_ciudad_de_las_bestias">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19388647-berenike?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19388647-berenike?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19388647-berenike?shelf=lang-spanish">lang-spanish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19388647-berenike?shelf=library-l">library-l</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19388647-berenike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2633919620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2166079680550471190">It's probably not fair that this is the first book by Isabel Allende that I've actually read (I had to pretend that I'd read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1574736.Las_Mujeres_En__La_Casa_de_los_Esp_ritus__de_Isabel_Allende' title='Las Mujeres En 'La Casa de los Espíritus' de Isabel Allende by Wojciech Osinski' rel='nofollow noopener'> La casa de los espíritus</a> in school but I never made it past page ~20).<br/>So I'm sad that this was a little disappointing.<br/><br/>Alex, a 15yo American boy, has to leave his family and go to the rainforest with his grandmother. They're part of an expedition that's supposed to investigate a mysterious 'Beast' that kills people and may or may not exist. A lot of other stuff happens, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText2166079680550471190" style="display:none">It's probably not fair that this is the first book by Isabel Allende that I've actually read (I had to pretend that I'd read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1574736.Las_Mujeres_En__La_Casa_de_los_Esp_ritus__de_Isabel_Allende" title="Las Mujeres En 'La Casa de los Espíritus' de Isabel Allende by Wojciech Osinski" rel="nofollow noopener"> La casa de los espíritus</a> in school but I never made it past page ~20).<br />So I'm sad that this was a little disappointing.<br /><br />Alex, a 15yo American boy, has to leave his family and go to the rainforest with his grandmother. They're part of an expedition that's supposed to investigate a mysterious 'Beast' that kills people and may or may not exist. A lot of other stuff happens, but basically <i>Alex, a fifteen year-old boy, has to save the indigenous peoples of the Amazon rainforest from a military invasion</i>. <br /><br />I know this is a book for children, but to be honest I'm still not really sure for what age. Even though the main character is actually 15, this felt more like a book for maybe 10 year-olds. A lot of things seemed a little over-simplified: people are either good or bad, everything will be alright if we're just nice to each other, you can understand any language if you just 'listen with your heart', etc. It felt more like a world-view for a 10yo to me. <br /><br />Also, the fact that this book included both the constant message 'protect the indigenous peoples' (basically in giant neon letters), and a lot of fantasy elements didn't really work for me. Either you're trying to portray the actual problems of indigenous peoples, or you're trying to write a fun fantasy story about magic mountains, dragons, ghosts and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[beasts who live for thousands of years <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />Though to be fair none of that might matter to a 10 year-old.<br /><br />I'm just hoping Allendes books for adults will be a little better when I finally get to them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2166079680550471190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3028520233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3028520233" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64261586-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572307602p2/64261586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3028520233?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/64261586-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060510329" href="/book/show/837674.La_ciudad_de_las_bestias">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3028520233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15368310721927524887">"While splashing with other young people, Alexander Cold thought that the world had never seemed so beautiful and that he would never be so free again ..."<br/><br/><br/>This book became special for me because it reminded me of a trip I made to the Ecuadorian Rainforest in the Amazon region many years ago under similar conditions. (I traveled with a team to make a photo book about THE HUAORANI PEOPLE that inhabit the Yasuni, the most biodiverse area in the world; the team was composed of a National Geographic </span>
  <span id="freeText15368310721927524887" style="display:none">"While splashing with other young people, Alexander Cold thought that the world had never seemed so beautiful and that he would never be so free again ..."<br /><br /><br />This book became special for me because it reminded me of a trip I made to the Ecuadorian Rainforest in the Amazon region many years ago under similar conditions. (I traveled with a team to make a photo book about THE HUAORANI PEOPLE that inhabit the Yasuni, the most biodiverse area in the world; the team was composed of a National Geographic photographer, a sociologist, a translator and I as a production assistant) <br /><br />Although the action of Allende's book takes place in the current Brazilian Rainforest in the Amazon region, we can remember that once that territory belonged to Ecuador so it is very similar to the rest of the current Ecuadorian Amazonian territory and the indigenous communities are very similar in both countries.<br /><br />This book made me live again experiences as if they were my own personal memories. Leaving aside the fantasy of the book, the rest of it seemed like a journalistic chronicle that faithfully portrays this area of the world. It is fascinating how Isabel Allende relate us us the customs, wisdom and spirit of the indigenous tribes that inhabit those areas as well as the the fauna, the flora, the landscapes, the beauty and the very spirit of these sacred and ashtonishing places. <br /><br />And above all it shows us the love that this brilliant autor feels for the jungle and indigenous communities, she restores to them the respect and dignity that they deserve and her work becomes highly educational and inspiring for those who never visited this area of the world, as well as a testimony for future generations of what is now and perhaps will disappear, along with a message of social and ecological awareness for those of us who believe that we can still work for a better world ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="15368310721927524887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3267534846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3267534846" />
    <a title="Helen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15413983-helen"><img alt="Helen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481815064p2/15413983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3267534846?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen" href="/user/show/15413983-helen">Helen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007146376" href="/book/show/149169.City_of_the_Beasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=competent-female-characters">competent-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=adventures">adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=fun">fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3267534846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5551591681000663634">I loved the bits where they were adventuring in the Amazon rainforest with Kate, Alexander's non-conformist and distinctly unmaternal journalist grandmother. <br/><br/>Kate really is the best thing in this book and I wish that she had more page time. After a big build-up of her character, she kind of fell out of the story and I feel that she was only there as a plot device to get an otherwise normal American kid on an adventure in the Amazon. <br/><br/>Though I have to say it's a story that's set up a lot better th</span>
  <span id="freeText5551591681000663634" style="display:none">I loved the bits where they were adventuring in the Amazon rainforest with Kate, Alexander's non-conformist and distinctly unmaternal journalist grandmother. <br /><br />Kate really is the best thing in this book and I wish that she had more page time. After a big build-up of her character, she kind of fell out of the story and I feel that she was only there as a plot device to get an otherwise normal American kid on an adventure in the Amazon. <br /><br />Though I have to say it's a story that's set up a lot better than the normal for this type of young adult adventure genre. <br /><br />The bits were this didn't do so well for me is when Alexander and Nadia were kidnapped by the People of the Mist. That all got to spiritual and dreamlike and I found it very hard to believe in what was happening. <br /><br />I'm all for a bit of magical-realism nonsense but it went too far here. <br /><br />I like the way it's written though and I really did enjoy the parts set in the company of the other Amazon adventurers. For me, it was worth reading for that alone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5551591681000663634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2697053516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8496322933411134944">Having seen the opening of this on a GCSE exam, I was intrigued and have been meaning to read this for ages.<br/>We begin with Alex in a difficult situation, knowing his mother is ill and expecting she will die. In order for her to get treatment, Alex is sent to stay with his grandmother, Kate. She’s a writer for National Geographic, about to head on a trip to the Amazon. Of course, in spite of being rather underprepared, Alex goes with her.<br/>The trip is beyond your wildest imaginings. Detailed account</span>
  <span id="freeText8496322933411134944" style="display:none">Having seen the opening of this on a GCSE exam, I was intrigued and have been meaning to read this for ages.<br />We begin with Alex in a difficult situation, knowing his mother is ill and expecting she will die. In order for her to get treatment, Alex is sent to stay with his grandmother, Kate. She’s a writer for National Geographic, about to head on a trip to the Amazon. Of course, in spite of being rather underprepared, Alex goes with her.<br />The trip is beyond your wildest imaginings. Detailed accounts of native life, exploration of ecological issues and magical elements involving mysterious creatures and events.<br />Suspend your disbelief, but this is an exciting read which also serves to get readers considering the environment and the impact we have on the world around us. More relevant than ever!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1Z4Qf2KdP4gqLQIY3N/S5JWfkOlUZCE3/IrWhLvqsRYmL6uS5+d1SHcE0poiZvByX+e1RgUNAshTP/ZttD6myg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lSXuS4St5/jFj1uXFOGGA+p+muVW9TUGyP+P2qtFLzNmlFWmAdetOJimixXqWKSVIAa/SgecFvlnSq8zpJE47w==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15108752976854073796">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at s</span>
  <span id="freeText15108752976854073796" style="display:none">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at several US colleges. She currently resides in California with her husband. Allende adopted U.S. citizenship in 2003.<br /><br /></span>
